Discovery of Ancient Tombs of the Liang and Song Dynasties in Nanxi, Sichuan 78

Two Pottery Coffins with Intact Lids Found in Liang Tomb

Song Tomb Has a Monument Inscribed with "Established in the 16th Year of Qingli"

Chongqing Dispatch: In recent years, Chinese people have repeatedly discovered antiquities, which is of great significance for archaeologists and those who study ancient culture. Recently, ancient tombs of the Liang and Song dynasties were also discovered in Nanxi County, Sichuan, and among them were also Wu Zhu coins minted during the reign of Emperor Wu of Liang, which can be described as a major contribution to archaeology. The circumstances of the discovery are recorded below for the reference of archaeologists.

Luo Boxi of Nanxi County is skilled in calligraphy and painting and proficient in epigraphy. Wherever he goes, he personally visits ancient temples and tombs. Last year, when he returned to his hometown from Qian, he heard that ancient tombs had been discovered in two places near Daqiao, about three miles outside the east gate of Nanxi. The villagers did not know about it and immediately covered them up. So, on February 24th this spring, he invited Zeng Mengliang, the director of the education bureau, and Zeng Jiguang, Zhong Chaoxu, and others to investigate. He inquired with local scholars and indeed found two ancient tombs. The Liang tomb had a deep and wide tunnel, stretching about a mile. There were two pottery coffins inside, with many pottery figurines of civil and military officials, and many pottery utensils. Wu Zhu coins were scattered around the coffin. There was nothing in the coffin except for the skull. After Mr. Luo's identification, this was a tomb from the Six Dynasties, and it had been excavated several years ago, as the lids of the two coffins were moved to the ground and the pottery fragments were scattered in the tunnel, which could not have happened if it had not been excavated. The Wu Zhu coins were quite large, minted during the reign of Emperor Wu of Liang, not the Wu Zhu coins of the Han Dynasty, so it was determined to be an ancient tomb of the Liang Dynasty without a doubt. The Song tomb was also discovered in previous years by Chen Yutu, a doctor of Chinese medicine. Because the tunnel was deep and wide, he was afraid to enter. This time, Mr. Luo and Mr. Zeng entered with lanterns for about a mile and reached the tomb gate. On both sides of the gate stood figurines of civil and military officials, tall and sturdy, about five or six feet tall. After a few more steps, turning left, there was a sacrificial hall. There were six rows of figurines of civil and military officials on both sides of the hall. Behind the hall were more than ten stone steps. Ascending the steps, a large monument stood tall, about seven feet high, with the inscription "Tomb of Zhou Qi, Grand Master of Military Affairs of the Song Dynasty." Beside it was a line of small characters that read "Established in the 16th Year of Qingli." Behind the monument was the burial chamber, with a stone door that was tightly locked. Looking inside through the window, a vermilion coffin gleamed brightly. Fearing that there might be snakes, they did not dare to enter. Mr. Luo and others lingered in the sacrificial hall for a long time before leaving. After Mr. Luo discovered the two tombs, he discussed with Zeng Mengliang, the director of the education bureau, to move the two pottery coffins, pottery figurines of civil and military officials, Wu Zhu coins, etc., to the library of the education bureau for future museum display. As for the vermilion coffin, because the figurines of civil and military officials were tall and the burial chamber was eerie, it could not be moved by a few people. It was planned to excavate on a small scale, and the stone walls of the sacrificial hall were still engraved with epitaphs, but the inscriptions were covered by moss and the characters were indistinguishable. It will be examined further in the future. According to Mr. Luo, pottery coffins are not uncommon, but the pottery coffins discovered in Sichuan Province are most valuable in three cases: (1) When Yang Zihui was governor of Sichuan, six pottery coffins were discovered in Wulidun, Chengdu, and are now stored in the provincial library, but none of them have lids, which is quite strange. (2) In the past, an American named Gevie Han discovered a pottery coffin in Yaan Tianquan, which had a lid but was broken, and is now stored in the museum of the Yibin Youth Society. (3) The two pottery coffins discovered this time have intact lids and can be called perfect. The material of the pottery coffins this time is ancient brown, six or seven inches thick. When struck, they make a clanging sound, very similar to metal and stone. If used to make inkstones, their value is immeasurable and cannot be compared with other pottery coffins. They are truly rare objects.

Page 8

Shi Yousan's Troops Transported to Heilongjiang Province 79

30,000 Surplus Troops Reorganized

Reorganized into the Heilongjiang Provincial National Defense Force

Harbin Dispatch: The reorganization of Shi Yousan's 13th Route Army and the issue of military pay were personally handled by Shi in Shenyang a month ago, consulting with Deputy Commander Zhang Xueliang at length. As Wan Fulin, the chairman of Heilongjiang Province, was in Liaoning, Deputy Commander Zhang invited Wan to discuss the matter jointly. The final decision was to reduce Shi's troops to three divisions, with the military pay to be borne by the central government and the Northeast at 200,000 each per month, and Heilongjiang to bear 100,000. The 30,000 surplus troops were to be transported to Heilongjiang and reorganized by Wan into the national defense force. Since the anti-Russian campaign, the national defense force has had many vacancies. For example, the three Class A brigades, the 2nd, 15th, and 17th, should have had more than 15,000 men each. After the war, after several recruitments and reorganizations, each brigade had only about 7,000 men. Heilongjiang Province has a sparse population, especially young men, so the recruitment has not been sufficient for a year. This time, the surplus troops from Shi's army are being reorganized, which is what the Heilongjiang authorities agreed to. Therefore, in mid-month, Wan summoned the commander of the 2nd Brigade, Su Bingwen, the commander of the 15th Brigade, Wang Yongsheng, and the commander of the 17th Brigade, Yu Zhaolin, to Shenyang, where Deputy Commander Zhang convened Wan Shi and the three brigade commanders to jointly discuss the number of troops to be reorganized into each brigade. After the decision was made, Wan returned to Heilongjiang on the 13th. At the same time, he sent four adjutants from the military command, Lin Shuchun and Zhang Baosen, with 50,000 yuan to Liaoning to transport the troops. On the 20th, a batch of these troops, totaling 760 soldiers and 50 officers, or 810 people in total, arrived in the provincial capital via the Tao'ang Railway. The rest will be transported successively, and are expected to arrive in Heilongjiang Province completely by late April. Currently, each of the 15th, 17th, and 2nd Brigades has a commissioner in the province waiting to lead the soldiers to their respective defense areas. It is heard that 4,000 men can be reorganized into the 15th Brigade, 6,000 into the 17th Brigade, and 7,000 into the 2nd Brigade. The rest will be reorganized separately into the 1st Brigade stationed in Heihe and the 2nd Cavalry Brigade stationed in Manzhouli Station. (25th)

Retrial Judgment of Gao Ying Case by the Jiangsu High Court 80

The case of Gao Ying, the former deputy consul in San Francisco, helping to traffic opium and dereliction of duty, was sent back for retrial by the Supreme Court. The Jiangsu High Court yesterday (30th) acquitted Gao Ying of the opium charges and sentenced him to one year and four months of imprisonment for dereliction of duty, with a fine of 1,400 yuan. Sun Yuan was sentenced to two years of imprisonment for the opium charges, with a fine of 2,000 yuan. The judgment has been delivered today (31st) at 5 pm and is recorded below:

Criminal Judgment of the Jiangsu High Court (Suit No. 1422 of the 19th Year) Appellant: Gao Ying, male, 36 years old, from Changle County, Fujian Province, former deputy consul of the Consulate General in San Francisco, USA, appointed defense lawyers Wang Youling and Liu Shifang. Appellant: Prosecutor of the Jiangning District Court Defendant: Sun Yuan, male, 41 years old, from Zhongshan County, Guangdong Province, former clerk of the Consulate General in the United States, appointed defense lawyers Li Zongqian and Lu Jianai. The above appellant Gao Ying and the defendant were charged with crimes such as opium and dereliction of duty. The Jiangning District Court issued the first-instance judgment on November 11, 18th year of the Republic of China. Gao Ying appealed the judgment, and the prosecutor of the original court filed an appeal against the part of the original judgment concerning the defendant. After the case was tried by this court, it was appealed again to the Supreme Court, which sent it back to this court for retrial. The judgment is as follows:

Main Text: The original judgment concerning Gao Ying and Sun Yuan is reversed. Gao Ying is sentenced to one year and four months of imprisonment for soliciting bribes for acts related to his duties, with a fine of 1,400 yuan. The number of days of detention before the judgment is determined shall be offset against the imprisonment at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. If the fine is commuted to imprisonment, it shall be calculated at a rate of three yuan per day, but the imprisonment period shall not exceed one year. He is acquitted of the opium charges. Sun Yuan is sentenced to two years of imprisonment for assisting in the sale of opium, with a fine of 2,000 yuan. The number of days of detention before the judgment is determined shall be offset against the imprisonment at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. If the fine is commuted to imprisonment, it shall be calculated at a rate of three yuan per day, but the imprisonment period shall not exceed one year.

Facts: Gao Ying was formerly the deputy consul of the Consulate General in San Francisco, USA. Sun Yuan was a clerk of the consulate. Sun Yuan had lived in San Francisco for a long time and was familiar with the overseas Chinese there. He also knew that, according to international practice, the luggage of consulate personnel and their families could be exempted from inspection upon entry. Therefore, in January of the 18th year of the Republic of China, when Gao Ying's wife, Gao Liao, returned to China from San Francisco, he asked a merchant named Shou Nanruoyun, whose surname was unknown, to ask Gao Liao to take advantage of this opportunity to transport a large amount of opium back to the United States for sale. At the same time, he asked Gao Liao to contact the Hong Kong smugglers Wen Yuxian and Shen Guang to purchase 2,299 cans of K-brand and Chang-brand opium paste, each can weighing about twelve taels and five qian. These were packed into eleven foreign boxes, with seals of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs of the National Government and signatures of the Consulate General in San Francisco affixed to the boxes, which were marked as Gao Liao's own luggage, along with keys and letters addressed to Sun Yuan and Shou Nanruoyun. Gao Liao took the foreign boxes and three pieces of her own luggage on the Tianyang Maru, a ship of the Japanese Mail Steamship Company, on June 14th of the same year, departing for the United States. She first informed Gao Ying of the date of departure and the name of the ship by letter, and Gao Ying informed Sun Yuan. On July 5th, when the ship arrived at the port of San Francisco, they went together to meet her. However, they were detected by the U.S. Customs, which detained all fourteen pieces of luggage carried by Gao Liao. After Gao Ying and Sun Yuan negotiated unsuccessfully to avoid inspection, the Customs opened the boxes and inspected them on the 8th of the same month, and found opium and letters entrusting the transportation of opium. The U.S. court arrested Gao Liao, Gao Ying, and Sun Yuan and sent them to Minister Wu in the United States, who sent them back to China and handed them over to the Jiangning District Court Prosecutor for investigation. It was discovered that in April of the 17th year of the Republic of China, while Gao Ying was serving as the deputy consul of the Consulate General in San Francisco, he had accepted the request of Chen Yi to introduce four Chinese laborers, Mei Guang, Mei Geng, Wu Zhuo, and Lu Huan, to go to the United States and disembark in San Francisco, with an agreed-upon reward of US$3,200, which was later changed to $2,600. On June 8th of the same year, Mei Guang and others arrived at the port on the Siberia Maru. Gao Ying boarded the ship to receive them and discovered that their passports had been altered and that the name of the abolished Mexican Consulate had been abused. He sent Mei Guang and others back to China. In addition to Chen Yi's separate defense, Gao Ying was prosecuted for assisting in the sale of opium and soliciting bribes, and Sun Yuan and Gao Liao were prosecuted for assisting in the sale of opium. After the Jiangning District Court tried the case, Gao Ying and Gao Liao were not satisfied, and the original prosecutor was also not satisfied with the part of the judgment concerning Sun Yuan, and appealed. After the case was tried by this court, it was appealed again to the Supreme Court, which sent the part concerning Gao Ying and Sun Yuan back for retrial. The reasons for the court's decision are explained in two parts below: (1) Regarding the opium part, Gao Ying in this case is the husband of Gao Liao. Although the opium boxes carried by Gao Liao were affixed with seals of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and signatures of the Consulate General in San Francisco, it has not been proven whether the signatures were from the Consulate General in San Francisco and issued by Gao Ying's hand, as the signatures were not affixed with seals. Moreover, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has not issued seals to foreign embassies and consulates for advance storage, as has been verified by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. Gao Ying, who was far away in the United States, cannot be held responsible for the seals of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs affixed by Gao Liao in China. The original judgment that the consulate seals were given to Gao Liao by Gao Ying in advance is highly speculative. After the U.S. Customs detained Gao Liao's boxes, Gao Ying went to the Customs to negotiate and repeatedly telegraphed Minister Wu to request exemption from inspection and release, which clearly showed that he was shielding her. However, since the appellant and Gao Liao are husband and wife, and it cannot be proven that the appellant had a common intention in advance, it is difficult to consider his subsequent efforts to remedy the situation as an act of assistance. Moreover, the repeated telegrams all stated that they were for the sake of preserving the national honor, so there is no crime. The original judgment that the appellant Gao Ying assisted Gao Liao in transporting opium, which constituted a violation of Article 15 and Article 6 of the Opium Prohibition Law, and was punished according to Article 271, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law, is flawed in both fact and law. The appellant's appeal regarding the opium part should be deemed reasonable. Furthermore, Sun Yuan, the defendant in this case, has lived in San Francisco for many years and is familiar with many overseas Chinese there. The letters from Wen Yuxian and Shen Guang to Sun Yuan carried by Gao Liao state: "I am now handing over the foreign boxes that the visitor is carrying, from No. 1 to No. 9, a total of nine boxes, to Brother Ruoyun for receipt, and two foreign boxes to Brother Shounan for receipt. Please send the foreign boxes to Brother Ruoyun and Brother Shounan for receipt as soon as they arrive (should be a typo for 'port'). Please telegraph the safety of each foreign box after they have been delivered." Wen Yuxian also sent Sun Yuan a separate letter stating: "Please personally open the foreign boxes and check that boxes No. 2 and No. 11 are delivered to Brother Shounan for receipt. Please deliver the remaining boxes to Brother Fu." It can be concluded that the defendant Sun Yuan has a close friendship with the Hong Kong opium traffickers Wen Yuxian and Shen Guang, and the San Francisco opium trafficker Shou Nanruoyun. Moreover, the 2,299 cans of K-brand and Chang-brand opium paste each weigh about twelve taels and five qian. According to the letters from Wen Yuxian and Shen Guang to Shounan, the cost of the K-brand is 70 yuan. If, as the defendant claims, he does not know Wen Yuxian, Shen Guang, or Shou Nanruoyun, how could he dare to entrust them to transfer opium worth millions of yuan? Moreover, since Wen Yuxian and Shen Guang entrusted Gao Liao to carry the opium, if there were no prior arrangements with the defendant Sun Yuan, Gao Liao could have directly handed it over to Shou Nanruoyun. Why would it be necessary to entrust the defendant to transfer it? The words "Telegraph the safety of each foreign box after they have been delivered" in the original letter clearly show that Gao Liao has no close relationship with Wen Yuxian and others. Her carrying of opium on behalf of Wen Yuxian and others, and the sending of opium to Shou Nanruoyun by Wen Yuxian and others, were all coordinated by the defendant. His assistance in the sale of opium is even more obvious. Although the defendant went to the ship to take care of the opium after it was transported, he was detained by the Customs and did not hand it over to Shou Nanruoyun. However, since there is sufficient evidence that he contacted Wen Yuxian and others in advance to traffic opium, he should also be held responsible for assisting in the sale of opium. The original trial did not study the details of the crime carefully and hastily acquitted the defendant, stating that the letters from Wen Yuxian and others carried by Gao Liao were merely one-sided requests and could not prove that Sun Yuan had any criminal intent. The prosecutor's appeal regarding this part is not unreasonable. (2) Regarding the dereliction of duty part, a letter from Chen Yi to the appellant Gao Ying stated: "I now have three or four people who want to go to the United States. Can I obtain diplomatic passports on their behalf? Can you receive them? If so, I will reward 1,000 yuan per person, and I will only take back a quarter." Another letter from Chen Yi to the appellant Gao Ying stated: "I received a telegram in the east stating that they have already boarded the ship and had to leave to pick up a letter in Shanghai stating that the Mexican identity could not be used. Fortunately, only one person used it. I don't know what the result will be. The amount could have been 3,000, but it was changed to 2,400. I have asked them to increase it to 2,600." This shows that Chen Yi requested Gao Ying to receive and introduce the four Chinese laborers Mei Guang, Mei Geng, Wu Zhuo, and Lu Huan to disembark in the United States. The appellant Gao Ying not only did not refuse, but also said that the Mexican identity could not be used, and instructed them on how to go to the United States. When the Chinese laborers arrived in the United States, the appellant Gao Ying falsely claimed that two of them were his private servants and asked Consul Gong to provide assistance. Moreover, the appellant admitted this clearly, and Sun Yuan also stated how he profited from it in detail. It can be seen that the evidence that the appellant and Chen Yi agreed on a reward to receive and introduce Chinese laborers to disembark is conclusive and leaves no room for argument. The Supreme Court has already made a clear judgment in its decision. The issue that should be investigated further now is whether the appellant's introduction of Chinese laborers to disembark is within the scope of his consular duties. Although Article 1 of the Regulations on Consular Officials states that the duties of consuls, consuls general, and vice consuls stationed abroad in the jurisdictional area are to develop the country's commerce and comfort overseas Chinese merchants, the consular duties stated in Articles 8 and 9 are not limited to commercial matters. Moreover, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs stated in a public letter to the original trial that "Consular duties are to protect overseas Chinese. Therefore, although there are no explicit regulations on receiving and introducing them at the port, it is something that should be done if it is actually necessary." It is difficult to say that receiving and introducing Chinese laborers to disembark is not a consular duty. Moreover, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs replied to this court that "Consular duties are originally to protect overseas Chinese. The United States has always restricted the entry of Chinese laborers. If the consul in charge determines that the situation requires it and sends personnel to the port to receive and introduce them, it is a duty that should be performed, and there is no need to issue any special orders." It can be seen that the appellant's introduction of Mei Guang and the other four people met the actual needs. The original trial found that the appellant Gao Ying's solicitation of bribes was not inappropriate, but his actions in office could not be said to be a violation of his duties. The original judgment's citation of Article 129, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law, and its application of the law, were flawed. Although the appellant's argument denying the facts of soliciting bribes is untenable, his attack on the inappropriateness of the original judgment cannot be said to be completely unreasonable.

In summary, in accordance with Article 385, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Procedure Law, the original judgment concerning Gao Ying and Sun Yuan is reversed and a new judgment is issued. Gao Ying is sentenced to one year and four months of imprisonment and fined 1,400 yuan for the crime of soliciting bribes for acts related to his duties, in accordance with the first part of Article 2, Article 128, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law, Article 3 of the Criminal Law Enforcement Regulations, Decree No. 160 of the National Government, Article 1, Paragraph 1 of the Regulations on the Crime of Betraying the Oath of Party Members, Article 5 of the Special Criminal Law and Other Criminal Sentencing Standards Regulations, with a one-third increase in the original sentence. He is acquitted of the other opium charges in accordance with Article 316 of the Criminal Procedure Law. Sun Yuan is sentenced to two years of imprisonment and fined 2,000 yuan for the crime of assisting in the sale of opium, in accordance with Article 2, Article 6, Article 15 of the Opium Prohibition Law, and Article 9, Article 44, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law. The number of days of detention before the determination of the judgment shall be offset in accordance with Article 64 of the Criminal Law. If the fine is not paid after compulsory execution, imprisonment shall be commuted in accordance with Paragraphs 3 and 4 of Article 55 of the Criminal Law. The judgment is hereby issued as in the main text.

Zhu Wenzhuo, Prosecutor of this court, presided over the hearing and performed the duties of the prosecutor. The court of appeal in this case is the Supreme Court. If any party is dissatisfied with this judgment, they should file an appeal with this court within ten days from the day following the delivery of the judgment, stating the reasons for dissatisfaction in writing. March 30, 20th year of the Republic of China. Lin Dawen, Presiding Judge of the First Criminal Division of the Jiangsu High Court; Judges Hu Shanyi, Zhang Bingci; Clerk Ma Yiqing

Fengxian 82

Su Wenxiang Has Escaped from the Bandit's Lair: Su Wenxiang, a villager from Qingcungang South Salt Lane in the Fifth District, who was kidnapped, has reportedly escaped from the bandit's lair after two months. However, the circumstances of his escape are strange, and many people are suspicious. According to the reporter's investigation, Su's family claimed that a few days before Wenxiang's escape (the night of March 14), twelve accomplices of the bandits came to their house and demanded a ransom of 10,000 yuan, otherwise they would tear up the ticket. They also forced Su's wife to negotiate the price herself. Unable to do otherwise, she was accompanied by a brave neighbor to the bandit ship (anchored in the sea about 30 miles away from Qianjia Bridge and Qin Gongtang). She saw Wenxiang tied up in the hold, suffering greatly. Just as she was about to negotiate, she saw three large ships sailing towards the sea, and the bandits suddenly panicked and waved her away. Not far from the ship, she heard rapid gunfire. However, whether it was a suppression operation by government troops could not be ascertained because she was anxious to escape. It was not until the afternoon of the 25th of this month that two patrol officers sent by the Zhejiang Water Police came to the town to report the news of the escape, and it was learned that it was the suppression operation of the 9th Patrol Team of the 2nd District of the Zhejiang Offshore Water Police. Su's family went to the newspaper yesterday and asked the county government to send police to accompany them to Jiashan, Zhejiang Police Team to identify him.

Changshu 84

Another Robbery Case in Xiaojian Township: At about 11 pm on the 28th, eight or nine robbers suddenly came to the home of Lu Qingqing, a farmer near Nandu Bridge in Xiaojian Township, Hongdou District. Speaking with a Hakka accent and carrying sharp weapons, they broke down the door. When Lu woke up from his sleep and tried to resist the robbers, he was immediately grabbed and forced to reveal the location of his hidden silver, and was beaten severely. After Lu begged, he was spared from harm. The robbers then sent two people to guard Lu and others, and the rest went inside to rob. They robbed for about an hour before leaving. After the incident, it was checked and it was found that more than a hundred silver dollars and several sets of clothes had been stolen. The Fisheries Representatives of Eight Counties Hold a Meeting in the Province: Hupukou in this county has a dense collection of fish markets. During the spring fishing season, thousands of fishing boats gather at this port for sales. The value of the fishing market in one season is about a million yuan. In recent years, due to the rampant sea bandits and frequent robberies on the Yangtze River, fishing boats dare not go fishing, so the Hupu fish market has been declining day by day. At the current spring fishing season, fisheries organizations have sent representatives to the provincial meeting to discuss remedies. Representatives from Tongzhou, Haizhou, Ganlu, Fuyang, Yancheng, Dongtai, Rugao, Changshu and other eight counties signed in. Ren Fei'an, a representative from this county, attended. The representatives proposed four key points, which are recorded as follows: (1) Salt Smuggling Problem: Regarding the fishery salt law and the method of changing the color and taste of salt, it has been announced on January 7 this year, so there should be no more private seizure and extortion. Small fishing boats can purchase salt in bulk at the salt fields, or purchase it separately from the local district office, fishery association, or fishery cooperative in accordance with the method of changing the color and taste. (2) Banditry Problem: Regarding banditry, two solutions were decided: a fundamental solution and a stopgap solution. A. The stopgap solution is to suppress the bandits before the small yellow croaker fishing season and enable the boats to go to sea for fishing with peace of mind. B. The fundamental solution is for the conference to appoint seven representatives from the Naval Department, the Coastal Patrol Office, the Security Office, the Jiangzhe Fisheries Affairs Bureau, the Civil Affairs Department, the Agricultural and Mining Department, and the Pacification Commissioner's Office to form a Maritime Defense Committee to organize a maritime security team. (3) Donation and Tax Problem: The issue of fisheries donations and taxes was not discussed at the meeting. Only Ren Fei'an, the representative from Changshu, submitted a written request to the provincial department to forward it to the central government for the implementation of fishery protection tax. It is now heard that the central government has submitted this case to the State Council for approval to exempt fisheries tax for discussion. (4) Problem of Encroachment on Fishing Grounds: Regarding foreigners arbitrarily occupying fisheries in the national territory, please request the central government to ask the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to separately resist. Regarding the Ministry of Finance, if Japanese fishing vessels do not have an export certificate from that country when importing, order the customs to prevent their import. Regarding the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, negotiate with the Japanese ambassador to prevent them from using the country as a fishing base within the national territory.

Great Fire in Xushi Town: Gu, a resident of Xushi Town in this county, runs a small cloth factory in the town, which is quite prosperous. At 10 pm on the 29th, a fire suddenly broke out on the chimney of the machine and spread to the houses. As the countryside lacked firefighting equipment, the fire spread for about an hour, destroying 36 houses, with an estimated loss of about 10,000 yuan.

Wuxi 85

A Doctor Causes an Accident While Giving an Injection: In Yangming Township, under the jurisdiction of the county, near Xiadian Bridge, in Zhang Alley, a farmer named Zhang A’bao’s son, A’gou, twelve years old, suddenly contracted acute meningitis the day before yesterday. They immediately invited Chen Zushou, a Western-style doctor from the Furen Hospital near Dagong Bridge outside the South Gate, to come to the village for treatment. Chen attempted a spinal tap, but somehow the needle suddenly broke off inside the skin. The doctor, realizing the trouble he had caused, immediately sent someone to carry A’gou to Puren Hospital to have the needle removed. Dr. Li Kele performed the surgery and extracted the broken needle. Unexpectedly, after the needle was removed, A’gou deteriorated and died yesterday morning. Zhang A’bao, deeply grieved by his son’s tragic death, had serious negotiations with Dr. Chen and carried A’gou’s body to the hospital, placing it in the doctor’s office. Later, others intervened and mediated, proposing to collect several tens of dollars to give to the family of the deceased for a coffin. It is not yet known whether the family of the deceased will agree.

Another Robbery and Assault Case in Nanyanshi: In the 11th District (Nanyanshi), in Di Ze Township, in Henghe Tou Village, a resident named Hua Yaozu, who made a living as a fortune teller, had accumulated some savings, which attracted the attention of bandits. The day before yesterday, around 1 a.m., a boat suddenly arrived with seven or eight bandits on board. Their faces were painted with colors, and they were armed with dangerous weapons. They swarmed ashore, broke open the Hua family's front door, and entered the house to rob them. Yaozu resisted the robbery and was struck in the head by the bandits. Fortunately, his injuries were minor and not life-threatening. Hua’s second daughter was also tied up with rope by the bandits. The bandits then went from room to room, overturning chests and cabinets, and looting extensively. After about half an hour, they left with their stolen goods, boarding the original boat and speeding away. Afterwards, an inventory revealed that gold and silver jewelry, clothing, and other items worth over 200 dollars had been stolen.

An Escaped Bandit from Jiangyin Arrested in Wuxi: Xiao Linshu from Shasha, Jiangyin, previously served as a leader of the Red Bandits and repeatedly participated in riots in various townships in Jiangyin. Last year, this bandit secretly fled to Wuxi and hid in the home of a certain family on Ba Lane near Tan Du Bridge outside the South Gate, where he made a living selling oil, bean curd, and vermicelli. Recently, Miao Lunqian, head of the Jiangyin Zhouzhuang Township Security Corps, discovered this and traveled to Wuxi the day before yesterday by boat to report to the County Police Brigade, requesting assistance in the arrest. Captain Wang, upon receiving the report, immediately dispatched Detective Team Leader Liao Dajin and detectives such as Hua Yao first to search and arrest Xiao Linshu. They brought him back to the team for questioning and sent him to the county government for detention yesterday, awaiting the Jiangyin County government to send officials with documents to Wuxi to take him back for interrogation.

Zhenjiang 87

Jiangsu Provincial Government Streamlines Land Taxes: The provincial government considers land taxes to be the largest source of revenue for the province.

However, there are many longstanding problems in various counties. Some landowners fail to pay taxes on their land, while others fail to report cultivated land for tax assessment. Streamlining these issues would pose many difficulties. First, there are no accurate statistics on the area of arable land in each county. Second, in the counties north of the Yangtze River, powerful landlords control the land and resist paying taxes. If the government were to strictly enforce the regulations, these landlords could incite tenants to cause disturbances and obstruct the process. Therefore, the current plan is to divide the entire province into several districts and begin streamlining the process in a few counties where the situation is relatively simple. The Land Bureau will work with the Finance Bureau to conduct a clear measurement of the land, using triangulation to determine the approximate area of the land. This will then be carefully reconciled with the actual amount of grain collected to identify discrepancies and gradually streamline the process.

Former Pixian Magistrate Sent to the Provincial Capital for Interrogation: According to a report from Wang Xipeng and other citizens of Pixian, the former magistrate of the county, Wang Lantian, was arrested in Jiangsu for owing public funds and failing to provide a clear accounting of his handover. They requested that the provincial government send someone to escort him to the provincial capital for interrogation. The Jiangsu Provincial Government immediately instructed Zou, the director of the Wuxian Public Security Bureau, to ensure that Wang was safely escorted to the provincial capital for interrogation. Director Zou, upon receiving the order, appointed Detective Team Leader Zhou Hongjiang to escort Wang to the provincial capital. The Finance Department sent a letter to the Zhenjiang County Government requesting that they detain Wang and ordering Magistrate Zhang to strictly pursue the recovery of the owed public funds.

Shangyu Shengbao Newspaper to Resume Publication Soon: The Shangyu Shengbao newspaper was previously accused by the county party headquarters of inciting ill feelings and violating party guidelines due to the publication of certain news items. The county party headquarters filed a complaint with the provincial party headquarters and requested that the newspaper be immediately closed down and the responsible personnel investigated. The provincial party headquarters, considering that the newspaper had a ten-year history and was the only media outlet in Shangyu, rejected the request and only imposed a two-month suspension for failing to register. Subsequently, after the newspaper explained its position, it was instructed to complete the registration procedures with the county party headquarters without any time limit and was permitted to resume publication as usual. The newspaper is currently preparing to register and will begin publishing as soon as the procedures are completed.

Important Educational News

Sun Yat-sen's Maxims Should Be Included in Textbooks 90

The Ministry of Education issued a special order to the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities, stating that attention should be paid to incorporating Sun Yat-sen's maxims into textbooks. The order cited a letter from the Training Department of the Central Executive Committee of the Kuomintang, stating, "The Training Department of the Hunan Provincial Party Guidance Committee submitted a report stating that the Hunan Provincial Training Conference resolved to recommend that the central government select Sun Yat-sen's maxims and the noble deeds of past sages that do not contradict the spirit of the Three Principles of the People and compile them into civic textbooks for schools at all levels in order to establish the central ideology of young people. The Ministry has reviewed the matter and believes that the intention is upright and appropriate. Therefore, we request that your ministry pay attention to selecting and incorporating these materials when editing textbooks related to party principles, Chinese language, and social sciences for schools at all levels so that the spirit of the proposal can be fully realized. We also hope that you will inform and instruct all relevant parties to comply."

The order was issued accordingly. In addition to separate orders, all publishing houses in the province and city are required to pay attention to selecting and incorporating Sun Yat-sen's maxims and the noble deeds of past sages that do not contradict the spirit of the Three Principles of the People when editing textbooks on party principles, Chinese language, and social sciences for schools at all levels. This is the order.

Training Directorate General Improves Military Education in Schools 91

Consults Ministry of Education to investigate secondary and higher schools to facilitate implementation.

The Ministry of Education yesterday issued an order to various provinces and cities to submit reports to the Ministry of Education by the end of May, based on a consultation from the Training Directorate General to the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities to submit the details of all public and private high schools and higher institutions by the end of May. The letter stated: "The implementation of military education in high schools and higher institutions has been ongoing for two years. While many schools have diligently followed the laws and regulations and made determined progress, a significant number have failed to comply or have not reported their implementation, even if they have implemented it. Currently, the Ministry is determined to ensure effective implementation. Therefore, we request that your ministry instruct the educational authorities in each province to investigate and report the following information for all public high schools and higher institutions under their jurisdiction, as well as private high schools and higher institutions that have been approved for establishment, regardless of whether they have implemented military training: the name of the school, its location, and the number of students, grades, and classes. Please compile and submit this information to the Ministry before the summer vacation so that we can take action." The Ministry has reviewed the matter and found that information on the names, locations, number of students, grades, and classes of public and private high schools and higher institutions in various provinces and cities has been reported to the Ministry and forwarded to the Training Directorate General for review. However, this information may be outdated due to the passage of time and may need to be updated. Therefore, in accordance with the consultation from the Training Directorate General, we urgently order that your department promptly compile a report in accordance with the attached format for all public and private high schools and higher institutions under your jurisdiction that have been approved for establishment and submit it to the Ministry by May 31 of this year for review and forwarding. This is the order.

Ministry of Education Extends Deadline for National Anthem Submissions 92

The Ministry of Education's call for national anthem submissions, originally scheduled to end at the end of December of the nineteenth year, received over 2,300 submissions. The Ministry held its third National Anthem Review Committee meeting the day before yesterday, attended by Political Vice Minister Li Shuhua, Permanent Vice Minister Chen Bulei, and others. The committee reviewed the submissions and concluded that a national anthem should represent the spirit of the nation, inspire national ambition, and encourage the patriotism of the people. Its effect is profound and of great importance. The best submissions received so far are still limited in number. Therefore, the deadline should be extended to the end of June of this year so that all submissions can be reviewed together to ensure careful consideration.

Municipal Education Bureau Orders Schools to Increase Labor and Production Activities 95

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau issued Instruction No. 252 to all middle and primary schools in the city (without separate documentation): "Instruction No. 471 from the Ministry of Education states that our country's middle and primary school education has not emphasized labor and production activities, resulting in graduates who are unable to engage in manual labor and have no vocational production skills. At a time when production is declining and people's livelihoods are in distress, school education must adapt to social needs to remedy the situation and avoid cultivating youth with excessive desires and a focus on personal gain, who lack the skills to earn a living after graduation. This is not only unhelpful to society but also exacerbates social unrest. These past educational shortcomings must be corrected. The education objectives of the Republic of China include 'enriching people's lives, supporting social survival and development, and developing national livelihoods,' and the implementation guidelines clearly state that 'general education must be based on Dr. Sun Yat-sen's teachings... and aim to cultivate citizens' livelihoods and improve national production capacity.' This is intended to correct past imbalances. All educational institutions must strictly adhere to these principles and not neglect them. In order to implement these education objectives and remedy educational shortcomings, the specific measures to be taken are listed below: (1) All public and private primary schools must strictly implement the work subjects as stipulated in the Ministry's Temporary Standards for the Primary School Curriculum. (2) All public and private junior middle schools must strictly implement the various subjects of agriculture, industry, and home economics as stipulated in the Ministry's Temporary Standards for the Junior Middle School Curriculum, taking local conditions into consideration. (3) All students in public and private middle and primary schools must participate in labor activities within the school. Special emphasis should be placed on production activities in various subjects. (4) Provincial, municipal, and county inspectors should pay special attention to the performance in agriculture, industry, home economics, and other subjects during inspections. (5) The Bureau should promote and advocate for labor and production education in various ways so that society and families fully understand the current trends in our country. All of the above points should be followed by the schools under your jurisdiction. If equipment is insufficient or teachers are lacking, funding should be increased and content enriched within a limited time, and teachers should be trained in various ways within the scope of your Bureau's responsibilities to achieve practical results. A report on the implementation should be submitted for verification. This is the order."

At 5:00 p.m., enter the city and visit the park, etc. At 6:30 p.m., take the express train from Wuxi Station. Arrive in Shanghai at 9:30 p.m.; (5) Note: Postponed by one week in case of rain. Beijing-Ping Aviation Scheduled 116

Shanghai-Yichang Aviation Officially Opens Yesterday

The China National Aviation Corporation's Shanghai-to-Yichang air route officially opened as scheduled yesterday. The company's pilot, the German Mr. Yost, flew the "Third Hankou" aircraft from Longhua Seaplane Airport at 7:00 AM yesterday, carrying passengers, namely the three people mentioned in yesterday's newspaper, and mail: 8 pounds to Yichang and 1.5 pounds to Shashi. The aircraft landed at each station on the schedule: Nanjing, Wuhu, Anqing, Jiujiang, Hankou, and Shashi. It was expected to arrive in Yichang at 5:10 PM that evening. The pilot will be replaced by Ericson when passing through Hankou.

The company's Beijing-Ping aviation route, which is under preparation, is also scheduled to officially start flying on April 15. However, it will only carry mail and will not carry passengers for the first month or two after opening. The flight schedule is as follows: Northbound: Nanjing departs at 8:30 AM, Xuzhou arrives at 10:30 AM and departs at 10:40 AM, Jinan arrives at 12:30 PM and departs at 12:40 PM, Tianjin arrives at 2:35 PM and departs at 2:45 PM, Beijing arrives at 3:30 PM. Southbound: Beijing departs at 8:00 AM, Tianjin arrives at 8:45 AM and departs at 8:55 AM, Jinan arrives at 10:50 AM and departs at 11:00 AM, Xuzhou departs at 12:50 PM and arrives at 1:00 PM, Nanjing arrives at 3:00 PM. There is one flight in each direction every day, and flights are suspended on Mondays.

French Aviators Pass Through Shanghai 117

Scheduled to Leave Shanghai at 6:00 AM Today

French aviators Bairdan and Meng Enxu flew a Farman monoplane from Paris to Tokyo on March 2. On March 18, they flew to Shanghai. The next day, they flew to Tokyo via Seoul. After staying for a few days, they planned to return to Shanghai from Tokyo via Osaka, Shenyang, Beiping, and Nanjing. It is known that the two aviators flew south from Beiping at 6:00 AM the day before yesterday, arriving in Beijing at noon. Fiasxu, the aviation counselor of the German embassy, was on the plane from Beijing to Beijing. The two aviators had lunch with French Minister Weili De in Beijing, and then left Beijing at 3:30 PM in the afternoon to come to Shanghai, arriving safely at Hongqiao Airport at 5:00 PM that evening. Originally scheduled to leave Shanghai yesterday morning to return to China along the original route, the French Consul General in Shanghai and the French Concession Police Superintendent held a banquet at the East Asia Restaurant to welcome them. At the same time, they received a report from the Xujiahui Observatory that the weather in the Taiwan area was not good, so it was decided to postpone it until 6:00 AM this morning to leave Shanghai. It is hoped to fly back to Paris within five or six days. The two aviators' round-trip flight between Paris and Tokyo was relatively smooth, except for being hindered by heavy fog in the Hong Kong area and being detained by the Japanese authorities in Seoul for a few days for flying over the Japanese military defense zone. If the weather in the south turns better this morning, they will first go to Hong Kong and then all the way back to France via Saigon and Hanoi. It is also heard that the purpose of the two aviators' flight this time is to open up a future air route from Paris to Tokyo.

Jianghai Customs Takes Over Foreign Warship River Moorings 118

Effective Today

Jianghai Customs issued a notice stating that the river moorings in Huangpu Port for warships from the United Kingdom, the United States, Japan, France, and Italy are causing obstructions to passing ships. Therefore, it has requested the navies of various countries to hand over the available river moorings to Jianghai Customs for unified management of the river surface. This will prevent collisions and accidents caused by merchant ships entering and exiting the Huangpu River. This matter was announced earlier and scheduled to begin on April 1st, with the Customs Commissioner taking over. Investigation revealed that river moorings No. 1 to No. 5 were for warships of various countries to moor, river mooring No. 6 was for China Merchants Bureau ships to moor, and river mooring No. 7 was for public ships to moor. Nos. 1 to 5 were all designated for foreign merchant ships, so foreign warships could moor freely. Nos. 8, 9, and 10 were for Japan Mail Company and Osaka Shosen, etc. Japanese warships coming to Shanghai all moored at river moorings Nos. 8, 9, and 10. Starting today, Customs plans to first take over river moorings Nos. 8, 9, and 10. Prior to this, the Japanese merchants were notified and negotiated. It is said that Japan Mail Osaka and other companies, although holding objections to this matter, had no choice but to prepare for the return due to the limitation of the situation, but they had to recover the price of the chains and other costs of setting up the river moorings from Customs. Negotiations are currently underway, and river moorings Nos. 1 to 5 must also be taken over and managed one by one in the shortest possible time.

Japanese Ships Disappear from Haizhou 119

The First Voice of Regaining Navigation Rights

Since the opening of Haizhou Port, Japanese ships initially dominated the shipping routes in the area. The route between Qingdao and Haizhou was almost exclusively operated by Japanese shipping merchants. Chinese ships only began operating after 1923, but under the pressure of Japanese ships, Chinese shipping merchants had no room for expansion. Japanese ships also often collided with Chinese ships. Until last year, after the central government negotiated with the Japanese side for a year, Japanese ships finally disappeared from Haizhou on February 21st this year. Our country regained its navigation rights, with Haizhou being the first voice of realization. The entire process and the current development of Chinese ships are recorded below.

Negotiations on Japanese Ships Stopping Navigation For nearly ten years, Japanese ships have been sailing between Haizhou, Qingdao, and Shanghai. Initially, few Chinese ships operated, resulting in Japanese ships dominating the Qinghai and Shanghai routes. Since the Japanese warships arbitrarily entered Haizhou the year before last, and because Japanese ships were hijacked by bandits, the Japanese navy arbitrarily landed, shot and killed Chinese people, and burned civilian houses, the central government began to protest and prohibit Japanese ships from entering the Haizhou inland area. Later, there was another incident of a Japanese ship sinking a Chinese ship. The central government negotiated again and sent warships to the Qinghai border to monitor Japanese ships, not allowing them to enter the inland area arbitrarily, otherwise they would be detained. To this end, Japanese ships changed their methods, specially preparing the blue sky and white sun flag inside the ship. When arriving at the outer port of Haizhou, they changed to hanging our national flag, posing as Chinese ships to mix into Haizhou. It was not until late February this year that customs were set up to prohibit them.

Haizhou Adds Branch Customs In the past, import and export taxes in Haizhou were collected by the Qingdong Tax Bureau. Japanese ships often evaded taxes. In February of this year, the Ministry of Finance decided to add Jianghai Branch Customs in Haizhou to specialize in collecting import and export taxes. Customs also sent patrol ships to patrol the outer sea of Haizhou to prevent tax evasion. Japanese ships that falsely hung our flag and secretly arrived in Haizhou to steal navigation were discovered by the branch customs several times and the ships were detained. Since February 21st, Japanese ships that falsely mixed in under false flags have not come to Haizhou.

Chinese Ships Are Developing More and More At present, the number of Chinese ships operating on the routes between Qingdao, Haizhou, and Shanghai, which were previously prohibited for Japanese ships, is increasing day by day. Initially, only Tongde, Hezheng, Yuelai, and other companies dispatched one or two ships. Now, China Merchants has also dispatched Tonghua, Yudada, and Northern companies, all of which have ships sailing to Haizhou. Last year, Dazhen Shipping Company was established, and there were formal scheduled liners dedicated to sailing between Shanghai and Haizhou. Huge docks were built in Dapu, and railways were built to directly connect to the Longhai Railway Station to facilitate freight transportation. After the end of the Northwest War, freight from Haizhou directly reached the three provinces of Shaanxi, Gansu, and Henan, and the volume of goods traveling back and forth increased day by day. Dazhen's Dayong and Ping'an ships are no longer sufficient. The company has decided to increase new shares by 500,000 to purchase two new ships to join this route, one named Jiyang and one named Ping'an. The plan is to expand the Shanghai-Haizhou route to 20 times per month, which is in progress.

Alliance of Three Shipping Companies Dazhen, Hezheng, and Chengxin shipping companies have agreed on a business alliance. Starting today, the export water freight from Shanghai to Haizhou will be increased by 20%, and the import water freight from Haizhou will be increased by 10%. The alliance treaty has been signed, and private price cuts are not allowed. If found, the first violation will be fined five times the collected water freight, the second violation will be fined ten times, and the third violation will be fined one hundred times. The fines will be used for charitable purposes.

Hidden Reefs Discovered on the Route In the middle of Haizhou, Shanghai, and Qingdao, near Wudaosha, at 122 degrees 12 minutes east longitude and 33 degrees 15 minutes north latitude, a new reef with a large area was suddenly discovered. It is very dangerous for ships traveling on the Qinghai and Shanghai routes. Customs has sent technicians to survey and map it, and notify each shipping company and list it on the new map. In addition, the body of the British ship Yingfa, which sank in August last year at the Linhong Port outside Haizhou, is gradually entering the waterway and obstructing navigation. The Longhai Railway Bureau plans to send personnel to blow it up to facilitate navigation.

Ministry of Finance Explains Measures for Levying Business Tax on Water and Electricity Industries 122

Water Supply and Sale Industries Separately Exempted from Tax

The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce received a telegram from the Ministry of Finance yesterday, stating: "In the case approved by Beiping Municipal Government No. 68, the Finance Bureau stated in its presentation that there are still doubts about the tax scope of banks and special companies, streetcars, electric lights, and tap water as stipulated in the General Outline and Supplementary Measures for the Collection of Business Tax. Please explain separately. The Ministry, in addition to investigating the General Outline for the Collection of Business Tax, stipulates in Article 1 that companies that have already paid income tax to the central government and those that have already been levied special taxes by the central government are excluded. The phrase 'refers to those who have already paid income tax or special taxes to the central government.' The Ministry has already established five explanation measures for circulation. Also, the banks and special companies mentioned in Article 1 of the Supplementary Measures should be taxed separately by the central government and are not within the scope of business tax in various provinces and cities. As for streetcars, electric lights, and tap water, each is a state-run enterprise and of course is not subject to business tax. If it is a private enterprise, streetcars and electric lights belong to the electrical industry, and the business tax rate shall not exceed 2/1000 of the business income. Water is the most needed and most easily consumed small commodity among daily necessities. Tap water industry, water sales industry, etc., are removed and exempted from tax." In addition to replying to the municipal government and instructing the Finance Bureau to be informed, it is hereby notified to you, Ministry of Finance, Jian Yin.

Paint Industry Requests Reduction of Business Tax 123

The Shanghai Paint Industry Association submitted a document to the central government. (Title omitted) "We humbly note that business tax is related to local tax revenue. All industrial and commercial sectors should fulfill their tax obligations. However, an excessive tax rate will inevitably hinder the ability to bear the burden. It is found that the association previously due to the rosewood and sandalwood in the member's woodenware items, the business tax regulations for the sale of goods issued by Jiangsu Province stipulates that the tax rate is 20/1000. The association considered that this regulation violated the framework set by the Ministry and sent a telegram to various ministries and courtyards of the central government for amendment last month. Later, the Ministry of Finance replied in a telegram on a certain day, stating that the business tax rate for the oil paint and rosewood industries should be amended separately and replied to the provincial government for transfer to the provincial Finance Department for compliance. The newspaper reported on the 26th of this month that the Jiangsu Province business tax regulations for oil and paint categories are 2/1000, while the Western furniture and rosewood industries are still taxed at 10/1000, which does not clarify the situation of the rosewood industry. It is found that although rosewood materials are produced in Siam and are clearly imported goods, the increase in import tariffs has increased several times compared to the past. When arriving in Shanghai and entering the trade (i.e., the rosewood trade), the trade should pay business tax. When the trade wholesales to the rosewood dismantling industry, business tax should be paid. When the materials are manufactured into various appliances and wholesaled to woodenware shops, manufacturing business tax must be paid. When the woodenware shop sells rosewood appliances, an additional 10/1000 business tax is added. A raw material such as rosewood is taxed no less than four times when manufactured into an item. It is not known that the general rules of taxation are that the tax rate of raw materials and goods needed by the country is reduced or even exempted from tax. The appliances made of rosewood are necessary for household use. Although their price is more expensive than ordinary miscellaneous wood, they are of high quality, durable, and last for decades or centuries. They are not as easy to rot as other miscellaneous wood, so they are popular with those who are proficient in household management. Most of the appliances made are used by Chinese people, and it cannot be regarded as a luxury item for tax purposes. Moreover, since rosewood is imported into China and manufactured into finished products, it is subject to heavy business tax. Woodenware merchants will be on the verge of bankruptcy, and the livelihood of tens of thousands of fellow workers will be completely cut off. The distress of being unsustainable is also understood by the authorities. It is regrettable that our country's industry is declining and production is backward, and the products made of rosewood are finely carved and exquisitely styled. They have won the most honorable awards in various national goods exhibitions and competitions in Europe and the West, which is enough to show the progress of our country's fine arts and art. The authorities should promote and support the development of the inherent culture. The government should give special awards to the rosewood industry. The name of the business tax should be based on the industry as a unit, and the goal of taxation should not be based on the goods. The association has previously telegraphed the Ministry of Finance to correct the situation, but it has still not been able to be considerate. Now that the opportunity is pressing, we have to express our feelings and request that the original business tax rate for Western-style woodenware and rosewood industries be paid special attention to when the conference passes it. In accordance with the original tax amount of the oil paint industry, the maximum limit is to reduce it to 2/1000, so as to cultivate national production and take care of the livelihood of merchants and people. This is also the reason for retaining the art of our country's inherent industry and maintaining the lives of poor workers. Accordingly, we intend to formulate a special reason for reducing the business tax on rosewood and other categories, and send a telegram requesting that it be approved for implementation. We are extremely eager to wait for orders. The Shanghai Paint Industry Association seals the document.

The Unified Tax Office Prohibits Extortion 124

The Ministry of Finance's Unified Tax Office issued a notice to various factories yesterday, stating that inspections of unified tax personnel sometimes involve extortion: "We hereby state that the collection of unified taxes at factories and customs is originally intended to facilitate merchants and people and eliminate accumulated malpractices. Merchants should comply with regulations and pay taxes without evading taxes or smuggling, and officials should be honest and impartial, and should not delay or extort. The director of this office has repeatedly warned and strictly prohibited this when he was in the Tobacco Unified Tax Office. Now he is also in charge of various unified tax affairs, which is busy and important. All subordinate officials should strive to improve their spirit and earnestly implement it. However, with the passage of time, they have become playful. Recently, it has been heard that inspection personnel still follow the old habits of the likin office and cannot avoid delaying and extorting fees for stamping procedures. Such behavior is superficially compliant but secretly violates the regulations, and it is extremely hateful. It should be investigated and punished severely. We hereby reiterate the ban and draw up a simple announcement for publication and posting to serve as a warning and rectify tax administration. In addition to issuing notices to all districts and offices for posting to inform the public, this announcement is hereby sent to your factory for reference. It is hoped that it will be posted together.

Local Cloth Sales Approved for Transport Permits 125

But No Tax Refunds If Heavily Taxed

The Ministry of Finance's Unified Tax Office replied to the Yarn and Cloth Association: "We hereby reply that we have received your presentation regarding the transportation and sale of artificial hand-woven cloth within the country. If the raw materials are woven from cotton yarn that has already been subject to the unified tax, it should be exempt from the unified tax and customs duties. However, during the period of tax-exempt transportation, customs duties are still collected by customs according to the usual practice, and it is still requested that customs stop collecting now. Also, rural households buy yarn in small quantities to weave cloth, and they have never obtained a tax certificate. What kind of procedures will be used for the inspection and release of local cloth for transportation and transshipment in the future, and please verify and order compliance, etc. It is found that the order to exempt existing cotton yarn and its direct woven products from the unified tax before March 31st and to pay customs duties as usual when passing through customs is an open case handled in accordance with the Ministry's order. All hand-woven cloth cannot prove that it is woven from new yarn that has been taxed after February 1st. During the period when inventory is abundant, it is treated as inventory and customs duties are levied accordingly, which is very fair. And the deadline for exempting inventory from the unified tax is approaching. From April 1st, customs will be able to verify the unified tax certificate for this item.

Page 10

[Hunger> Third Edition (10)

Local cloth can be verified with a unified tax certificate and released, and no tax will be levied again. The deadline is already very short, and all merchants should strictly comply with the regulations and must not be trivialized in order to maintain the original case. As for rural households buying yarn in small quantities and weaving it by hand, it is claimed that there is no way to obtain the original cotton yarn tax payment certificate, and it is difficult to prove that the raw materials have been subject to the unified tax. However, in order to show special consideration, this office will temporarily allow everyone to apply for a transport permit so that customs can verify it and release it. However, all hand-woven cloth, whether it is transported and sold abroad or in non-unified tax areas or in unified tax areas, will not be refunded if heavily taxed, to indicate restrictions. A stamp stating "Hand-woven cloth cannot be refunded" is added to the transport permit to identify it. In addition to instructing all bureaus to comply, we hereby reply for your reference."

Please add specialized commissioners

The congress dues and travel expenses for the delegates are also requested to be issued. The following is a record of the telegrams:

Telegram requesting the dispatch of specialized commissioners: To the Nanjing Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Ministry of Finance, Ministry of Industry, Ministry of Transportation, and Ministry of Railways: The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce previously participated in the International Chamber of Commerce in the eighteenth year of the Republic of China, dispatching ten representatives and three specialized commissioners to attend the Fifth Congress of the International Chamber of Commerce. The Sixth Congress of the International Chamber of Commerce is scheduled to be held in Washington, D.C., on May 4th of this year. After the association was organized and established, it formally telegraphed its participation and nominated Bei Songsun, Guo Bingwen, Li Guoqin, and others as representatives. It is now found that the proposed agenda for this congress includes (1) measures to prevent the decline in silver prices, (2) the issue of claims against European debts, (3) the issue of German reparations, (4) the issue of gold hoarding by the United States and France and the concentration of gold, (5) the issue of global production restriction agreements, and (6) the issue of tariff barrier removal. The decline of our country's foreign trade and the losses from the high cost of gold and the low value of silver necessitate the dispatch of more representatives and specialized commissioners to attend and propose discussions on relief methods. In addition to the three representatives already nominated by the association, we hereby inform your departments, earnestly requesting approval to add representatives and specialized commissioners to attend, so that officials and merchants can cooperate and work together. We also hope for a reply to facilitate statistics on the number of attendees and budget for travel expenses. This is of utmost importance. Chen Guangfu, President of the Chinese Branch of the International Chamber of Commerce, and Guo Bingwen, Vice President, respectfully bow.

Please examine and approve the record and issue an official seal for credibility. The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce of the Republic of China previously participated in the International Chamber of Commerce in the eighteenth year of the Republic of China, dispatching representatives and specialized commissioners to attend the Fifth Congress of the International Chamber of Commerce, and preparing to organize the Chinese Committee of the International Chamber of Commerce. The articles of association have been attached and submitted for record, and a request has been made for financial assistance. Upon investigation, the articles of association of the International Chamber of Commerce seem to be based on the old system, which China should follow. Therefore, the name "Chinese Committee of the International Chamber of Commerce" has been changed to "Chinese Branch of the International Chamber of Commerce," and it was organized and established on February 7th of this year. Chen Guangfu was appointed as President, Guo Bingwen as Vice President, and Lin Kanghou as Secretary-General. They have taken office and telegraphed the International Chamber of Commerce to report formal participation. We hereby submit a report to your government and departments regarding the organization and establishment, requesting your examination and approval of the record and the issuance of an official seal for credibility. Please grant an approval order for compliance, as it is in the public interest. In addition to separate submissions, we respectfully submit this to the National Government, the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and the Ministry of Industry.

Request for dues: A report requesting the allocation of government subsidies of 30,000 silver dollars for the Sixth Congress of the International Chamber of Commerce. The expenses of the International Chamber of Commerce were previously submitted by the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce of the Republic of China to the National Government, requesting a subsidy of 30,000 silver dollars for congress fees in the year of each congress and 10,000 silver dollars for annual expenses. An order was received to collect the congress fees for the eighteenth year.
